    <li> shaved off piece of meat</li>
    <li> The Feather \\&quot;Popular\\&quot; twist-to-open (TTO) razor is a good entry-level product for those interested in trying out traditional shaving.  There are other currently manufactured TTO razors on the market, but the quality is generally hit or miss.  Despite the light weight and partial plastic construction, in many ways this is better than razors from Parker that cost the same or more.    The best feature of this razor in my opinion is the more sloped profile of the cutting head.  The vintage safety razors from Gillette had a head like this, before they moved to a more \\&quot;slim\\&quot; profile in the early 1960&#x27;s, ostensibly making it easier to shave the tight areas under the nose.  But in keeping this \\&quot;fatter\\&quot; head, the Feather Popular is a very good choice for those with sensitive skin, since it requires a less-steep blade angle.  The drawback to this, combined with the razor&#x27;s overall light weight, is that the shave is very mild.  But if paired with a very sharp blade like Feathers (probably the sharpest blades currently available by some stretch), it&#x27;s possible to get a close, smooth shave with no irritation.  And it&#x27;s also worth noting that blade alignment in the cutting head is even on both sides.  You&#x27;d think this goes without saying, but you&#x27;d be surprised at how many modern TTO&#x27;s don&#x27;t get this right.  The blade is also locked securely in place.    However, given the Feather company&#x27;s high standards, I have to wonder why 85% of the razor is plastic, including the entire lower portion of the cutting head.  This affects the razor&#x27;s glide a bit and shaving cream/soap scum is more noticeable on the black plastic over time.  But that&#x27;s more of a cosmetic concern and it doesn&#x27;t mean the razor is \\&quot;cheap\\&quot; by any means.  This is something that will probably last on the order of 50 years with proper care.  And with 6 to 7 shaves per blade, with less irritation than modern cartridge systems, it&#x27;s a smart choice for men who are curious about wetshaving.      I still think the Lord L6 razor (also available on Amazon) is the best choice for a cheap starter razor, but you could certainly do worse than the Feather Popular.</li>
    <li> I think I found my new favourite razor.</li>

    <li> Several months ago after experiencing a bad rash on my neck, which was made worse by shaving, I elected to try a different razor type.  I went with the double edge Lord L6.  I liked the shave but not the razor.  It was rather cumbersome to remove/replace the blade.  I ended up going on the auction site and I obtained a few old Gillette&#x27;s. Each requiring a slightly different technique due to their size and weight.  Then I stumbled across this thing.  Although inexpensive (not cheap), it in many ways offers the best of the above mentioned razors.  The handle is thick like the fat boy making for easy holding, it has a long handle and great styling like the black beauty, but still is very light weight like a disposable. I don&#x27;t think the light weight aspect can be addressed strongly enough.  With a really sharp blade like the  feather, you need a very light touch.  When you have a heavy razor, it&#x27;s easy to bear down harder than you should , and inadvertently nick your self.  This razor makes that less likely.  At first I was really disappointed in this razor.  I thought it was cheap , particularly seeing the inside made of plastic, and didn&#x27;t believe it would last very long.  What I previously viewed as a shortcoming I now see as a very distinct advantage. Although I enjoy using the old Gillettes, whenever I come back to this razor I always find myself more impressed by it. A few notes on other things.  I found a better price on the auction sites for feather blades, particularly in lots of 100. Although I love the sharpness, the feather blade is very unforgiving.  If your skin is not smooth it will remove anything in it&#x27;s path, hence the need for a VERY light touch.  I am considering trying Astra blades, which may not be quite so lethal. It&#x27;s important to wash your face well before adding any shaving cream or soap. Apply a good aftershave afterwardsto clean up any small nicks you have, then a good skin cream such as Cetaphil moisturizing lotion.  As someone with very sensitive skin, I&#x27;m forced to pay a bit more attention to these details, and hope perhaps this helps others in the same boat.Likewise I appreciate your tips. Update 7/1/2016 Still using the original razor, although I did buy a spare about a year or so ago. Sometimes when I travel I take a disposable double edge razor. One month of Fusion cartridges would equal what I paid for this Feather razor and it&#x27;s two included blades.     <li> I ordered this razor as a travel piece that I would not cry over if lost for any reason ... I&#x27;ve grown attached to my Weber razor and no longer risk it to the TSA folks, they can be moody in some parts of the world.&lt;br /&gt;This razor is a fine tool!!  I have been using DE razors for over 60 years and this fine instrument holds it&#x27;s own against any as far as shaving quality.  Obviously, for the price, it&#x27;s not going to compare with my all stainless, polished Weber in appearance but that&#x27;s not what we&#x27;re discussing here.&lt;br /&gt;The safety bar on this razor would allow a moron to wack away at their face without much threat.  I have never so much as nicked myself with this gentle razor even when violating all the rules and shaving against the grain.  I have a medium heavy beard and it&#x27;s no push over!!&lt;br /&gt;Regarding the mechanics of this tool here is what I recommend.  After using it for over a year this works.  I keep the main supporting pin and the tightening mechanism lubricated with a drop of 3 in one oil about once a month.  I clean the razor a little every three or four days.  I NEVER TIGHTEN THE PLATFORM CAP MORE THAN FINGER &#x27;SNUG&#x27;!!!!  That&#x27;s all that is necessary to perfectly seat the blade that is precision placed by the guide bar.&lt;br /&gt;I use cheap, $2.00 a can, Barbasol shaving cream because it easily clears with a splash of water from any DE razor.  This is not true of some gels and some other shaving potions.  I loosen the mechanism after shaving and do not apply any pressure again until the next shave ... this preserves the mechanism.  This razor&#x27;s moving parts are all stainless and, yes, they are not hefty but that makes no difference.  Treated with some care, don&#x27;t screw down on the lifting mechanism, this razor could last someone for years and years!!!!&lt;br /&gt;No, it is not my Weber Stainless but it is one fine, forgiving, well constructed, for it&#x27;s purpose, razor!!!  You will never go wrong for the price here and you won&#x27;t go wrong with it mechanically unless you unnecessarily stress the head my jacking down on the lifter!!!</li>

What I really like is not having to pay $4 a blade for Fusion or Gillette.  I switched about a year ago to Harry&#x27;s but those blades turn out to be about $2 each. would twist the butterfly mechanism closed so far that the blade would be completely bent in against the head, which did not provide a very close shave. i would twist it open to the point that the blade lay flat and loose inside the head, and the shave would tear up my rough face. eventually i settled on a position where the blade would be slightly bent, and i get a great shave each time.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;the razor has held up so far just fine. all the parts still function correctly, and i have not had any issues with corrosion or deterioration. all the plastic bits are still fully intact as well. i have noticed that the razor likes to collect soap scum, but with a bit of scrubbing on it once a week or so, it remains pretty clean and doesn&#x27;t suffer from build-up. since this is my first razor, i cannot offer comparisons to others. however, this razor could stand to be a bit heavier. i can see how a heavier razor would offer better balance and smoother operation.&lt;br a bit every few minutes, because it tends to work its way loose over time.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;that being said, i still definitely recommend this razor for the budget-conscious consumer. i may     <li> Lets start by acknowledging that this is not intended to be, marketed as (or priced) as a first-class razor. Its advertised as combining affordability with performance, and thats probably about right. If you want twice the razor, get yourself a nice Merkur for about twice the price (search for Merkur Double-Edge Razor right here on Amazon.com; youll find several nice ones). That said, if youre just starting out in Double Edged razor shaving and dont want to spend a lot, or if youre looking to take your wet-shaving on the road and just want a lightweight DE razor to toss into your travel shave kit, this razor is worth the money.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;On the plus side, if you use a good blade (I use Feather blades) this razor will give you a decent shave.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;A minus to me - and it may not be a negative to everyone - is that this razor holds the blade at a much less aggressive angle than the Merkur razors I use. Look at the pictures of the Merkur razors here on Amazon and youll see a pronounced curve to their tops; that curved top closes down on the blade, bending it over to achieve a fairly aggressive cutting angle. That angle seems to give me a closer shave. This Feather razor is flatter at the top, consequently it does not bend the razor blade as much and the cutting angle is not as great. Again, the sharper angle is the one my face prefers; this razors angle may feel better to you. (Ive looked at some of the other reviews since I first wrote this, and indeed other reviewers DO feel that this razors angle works better for them. So it really is a matter of personal preference.)&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The other thing to be aware of is that this is, as advertised, a razor made largely of plastic. That saves weight (again, good for travel), but feels less solid in your hand - because it is. Thats not necessarily bad, it just is what it is.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;This is a moderately priced DE razor, and it will give you a moderately good shave. I recommend it for those who may not want to spend a lot on their first DE razor, or for experienced DE shavers who may looking for a lighter razor and are willing to give up a little bit of closeness in their shave in return. I use if for that reason, and its not a bad tradeoff.</li>

    <li> I&#x27;ve only ever used a cartridge razor or occasional electric so this is my first safety razor.     <li> I decided to switch back to DE safety razors after about a 20 year hiatus due to the constantly escalating price of my Fusion cartridges. With the \\&quot;fog of time\\&quot;, I actually don&#x27;t remember why I switched to cartridges in the first place; but, boy, am I happy that I switched back! This razor is very lightweight and simple, but does its job really well with zero nicks and cuts with my first two shaves. I used the stock Feather blades that came with the razor and they seem to pair up well together. The blade is angled quite a bit and the razor is very \\&quot;non-aggressive\\&quot;. I found that I can shave much faster than I can with my Fusion razor and I get a closer, smoother shave much quicker. I use the razor both with the grain and against it (yes, I know that it is not recommended) and it seems to work really well both ways. One minor quibble is that the handle feels a bit short in my large mitts and the razor feels slightly top heavy compared to my old metal DE razors whose handles were more heavy, which gave them a bit more balance. However, this did not detract from the use of the razor in any way.    After this experience, I cannot see myself going back to my cartridge razor anytime soon (other than instances where TSA will not allow me to carry DE razor blades in my carry-on luggage!)     <li> Great product, great price. Might just be my face/beard, but this one shaves wonderfully for mine, while more expensive ones did not. Made me a fan of Feather products and blades.</li>
    <li> I first used a DE razor as an adolescent in the 70&#x27;s but soon the proliferation of disposables and the development of cartridge razors made them obsolete. As the decades went by I went from cartridge blades featuring 2 blades to 3 blades to the ridiculous and over priced 5 blade models, all the while paying ever increasing prices for those designs, up to the tune of $5 a blade. Then I had begun evaluating the expense of these \\&quot;miracle\\&quot; cartridge shavers and decided to try the DE shaving system once again, if not for merely nostalgia then to pay only ~.35 cents a blade versus five bucks.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;My first attempts failed miserably. I ended up with a satisfactory shave on the face, but on the throat and below the jaw I found shaving with a DE razor more akin to losing a battle with a sword wielding Ninja. I went back to cartridges for some years after, deciding \\&quot;nostalgia\\&quot; shaving technology was best left in the past where it originated.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;After hearing a co-worker talk about his satisfaction with DE&#x27;s and more research on the &#x27;net, I decided to attempt this \\&quot;new-old\\&quot; shaving system once more. Realizing my past failures, I knew I needed to do something different. My skin is not super-sensitive, but not sheet leather either. What had I done wrong before? I soon began to find the answers.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The problem I realized, is that cartridge razors teach you to shave \\&quot;incorrectly\\&quot;. Due to the fact they are essentially a blade or set of blades that are set into a box at a 30-40 degree angle or so (that&#x27;s my guess), you are forced to place the shaving implement flat against your face for them to work. Couple that with their tendency to accumulate junk between the blades and you must increase pressure to maintain sufficient blade-skin contact. They do work adequately when employed as their design dictates, but the technique they force you to use is disastrous if transferred to a DE razor.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I purchased this Feather model DE and wasn&#x27;t particularly impressed with it out of the box. Though well made in appearance, it was predominantly plastic. Aren&#x27;t DE razors supposed to be metal and super heavy? The handle of about 4 inches appealed to me though. I knew with use of razors with stubby 3 inch handles I did not have the degree of control (unbalanced to me) I needed. I loaded a brand new Feather DE razor blade in it and vowed the next morning I would shave with it, but in doing so throw out the window everything the cartridge razor system had taught me. I knew I would have to \\&quot;re-learn\\&quot; how to shave to make this system work.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;For one, the plastic construction actually works for me much better than the purported benefits of the heavy weight metal models by increasing my control of the unit. What I discovered was that the additional handle length acted less as a gripping surface and more of a counter balance to the weight of the blade bearing head as I held the razor primarily between thumb, index and middle fingers. I decided I preferred the butterfly opening top instead of the removable cap some designs sport.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Use a good shave cream. This is as personalized a choice as any, but a good quality shave cream is essential. Quality shave cream is a crucial friction reducer as the blade glides over skin. I prefer a canned cream such as Barbasol Aloe. Avoid the gimmicky, razor clogging gels.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Blade angle. I maintained as well as possible a blade-to-skin angle of approximately 40-ish degrees, maybe slightly less.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;NO PRESSURE. I repeat, none. Cartridge razors encourage the application of pressure to maintain blade-skin contact and this is a bad habit cartridge blade users often carry over to their first efforts with a DE razor. There is no need to apply pressure with a DE razor. The blade is there, not inset below a box frame, so it does its work without requiring any pressure to efficiently slice your stubble.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Short, even strokes. With box cartridge razors I had developed thebad habit of dragging the razor from ear to chin in one continuous stroke. Do not do this with a DE razor. Gradually work your way down (or up) in short, light strokes, maintaining and adjusting your blade angle as appropriate.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Second passes. Never make a second pass (such as against the grain) without re-applying shave cream to that area. Another bad habit I had developed with cartridge razors I found I needed to break in order to succeed with a DE razor.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Whenever possible, stretch skin flat and taught. When this is more difficult to do (around the throat in particular), make your strokes even MORE light and short. This technique alone will reduce or eliminate the vast majority of nicks and abrasions.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Take your time! If you don&#x27;t have the time, wait until you do to practice. Though once you have committed your technique to memory it will become second nature, avoid the initial temptation to treat DE shaving like it&#x27;s a 2 minute and done cartridge razor shaving session.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;When choosing a DE system, expect to have to buy a few different brands of razors, blades and creams before you hit on the combo that works best for you. I did, and I stopped looking after buying this Feather and the Feather blades.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I am now done with cartridge razors. Some may find the transition is easy, others will not, but no doubt when used correctly they are a highly efficient and extremely cost effective alternative to the \\&quot;miracle\\&quot; super duper, twisting, rotating, vibrating, pivoting razor marketing gimmicks pitched to shavers around the world at a substantial expense to your shaving budget.ke. Do not do this with a DE razor. Gradually work your way down (or up) in short, light strokes, maintaining and adjusting your blade angle as appropriate.    Second passes. Never make a second pass (such as against the grain) without re-applying shave cream to that area. Another bad habit I had developed with cartridge razors I found I needed to break in order to succeed with a DE razor.    Whenever possible, stretch skin flat and taught. When this is more difficult to do (around the throat in particular), make your strokes even MORE light and short. This technique alone will reduce or eliminate the vast majority of nicks and abrasions.    Take your time! If you don&#x27;t have the time, wait until you do to practice. Though once you have committed your technique to memory it will become second nature, avoid the initial temptation to treat DE shaving like it&#x27;s a 2 minute and done cartridge razor shaving session.    When choosing a DE system, expect to have to buy a few different brands of razors, blades and creams before you hit on the combo that works best for you. I did, and I stopped looking after buying this Feather and the Feather blades.    I am now done with cartridge razors. Some may find the transition is easy, others will not, but no doubt when used correctly they are a highly efficient and extremely cost effective alternative to the \\&quot;miracle\\&quot; super duper, twisting, rotating, vibrating, pivoting razor marketing gimmicks pitched to shavers around the world at a substantial expense to your shaving budget.</li>
    <li> I decided to go back to the old way of shaving with mixing my own shaving cream with a cake and a brush, and shaving with the type of razor my dad and his dad used.  All of the new high tech razors with their multiple blades and high costs aren&#x27;t worth the money.  This razor works perfectly and provides a better and closer shave than anything I&#x27;ve tried.  It is priced right for someone wanting to get back to the old style (there are others on-line costing much more).  The only thing I would do differently is order addition blades when ordering the razor.  It comes with blades but only two in the package and you&#x27;ll need others on hand.  I&#x27;m still on a learning curve with it all but it seems a week of daily shaves is the life of a blade - the sharper they are, the better the shave.</li>

    <li> I have VERY sensitive skin and after having tried everything to stop razor burn (which for me lasted several painful days after a shave) I decided to make the change from using disposable razors with the various pre-shave/post-shave/supermarket shaving gels to an old fashioned pre-shave, cream applied with a boar brush, and this DE safety razor from Feather. Lock your wrist, use your shoulder to move it up and down an inch or so at a time and turn it/rinse it frequently. I really like the butterfly twist open type makes it simple and easy to replace the blades. The safety razor also comes with a useful plastic see through case that also holds five blades.</li>
    <li> I have shaved with an electric shaver/razor and have tried several types of \\&quot;cartridge\\&quot; multi-blade razors, including recent 5 blade contraptions that to me were uncomfortable to shave with. The companies that make these cartridge razors increase the price for every new blade they add. It seems at some point the quality of the shave became less important and the sales of ever more expensive cartridges became the goal.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;And they are all different, having various parts that snap together that are not compatible(between different razors). Sometimes looking at the cartridges I wondered whether they were designed to fail prematurely, spacing between the blades in some is limited and/or some plastic part would cause hair to become jammed in the crevice between the blades making the cartridge difficult to use, causing discomfort to my skin, and just failing to shave properly - result would be a need to replace the cartridge after a few uses. The price of cartridges did not go down when I used them regularly. I tried both store brand and \\&quot;name\\&quot; brand cartridge razors.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;During the Summer of 2011 I decided to give electric shaving a new try after using a Braun shaver/razor for some time with disappointing results about a decade ago. I bought a \\&quot;cheap\\&quot; Norelco 7310XL and used that together with Afta Pre-Electric lotion until recently. It gave good results, but frequently left me with razor burn on my neck(even after using the lotion).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Electric shaving in my opinion has its strengths. The Norelco shaver/razor uses long lasting blades that are replaced after 6-12 months. This helps reduce waste and cost. The bottles of lotion lasted me several months and are recyclable. If the shaver/razor is well made and lasts a long time overall waste is reduced. That can&#x27;t be said for \\&quot;disposable\\&quot; razors that just fill up landfills, cartridge razors are only slightly less wasteful. I was looking for a shaving product that produces low amounts of waste, producesgood results as far as shave quality, and would be relatively cheap(affordable).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I decided to give Double Edge Safety razors a try together with \\&quot;wet\\&quot; shaving. This was all new to me, my grandfather used to shave this way. My father still has an old DE razor he received as a gift, with an old blade(which is like 20 years old) he virtually never uses. I wanted a newer one with a long handle. I decided to try this Feather razor with a Van Der Hagen brush, bowl, and soap kit.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;My initial cost was around $30. Which was slightly more than the cost of replacing the blades on the Norelco shaver/razor. I did not want to spend a lot of money for something that I was not sure I would use for a very long time. I really did not want to buy a more expensive Parker, Merkur, or Edwin Jagger (etc.) razor so I went with the more affordable Feather. It likely has a lower price because it has more plastic parts(than other DE razors), which will likely reduce the razor&#x27;s service life. Although the moving parts appear to be made of metal(from the outside).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I was not really expecting much in shave quality, after all, I thought to myself, this is an \\&quot;older generation\\&quot; of shaving technology.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The Feather razor arrived packaged with 2 Feather Hi-Stainless blades, which seem to have a reputation for being the \\&quot;sharpest DE blade\\&quot;. Many claim that the Feather blades are almost dangerous for beginners. I did not experience anything life threatening with these blades.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;This razor is a \\&quot;butterfly\\&quot; design/type. Meaning the \\&quot;head\\&quot; opens up(into 2 identical metal pieces) through internal machinery, which is moved by a rotating mechanism on the upper part of the handle. The head is not removed like on certain (more basic) 3 piece razor designs. This makes replacing the blade a much simpler task. There is a metal \\&quot;retainer\\&quot;(best way to describe it) that holds the blade in place and divides the head into 2 distinct sides.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The handle is mostly plastic with a good grip surface which prevents you from dropping the razor. The connection point between the head and handle is also made of plastic.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I did a few practice strokes on the neck with an un-even amount of shaving soap lather. After several shaving sessions I came to the conclusion that the Feather blade just seemed wrong for my skin(dry and easily irritated) and hair type. It left me with mild razor burn that went away after a few minutes, but made shaving my beard area somewhat uncomfortable. On my 3rd or 4th shaving session I tried a Wilkinson Sword blade, this too felt uncomfortable, plus I cut myself more often than I had with the Feather blade.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I next moved to an Astra blade, which did not cause me as much discomfort around my beard area although I was left with some cuts. After I started using a glycerin based soap the shaving experience improved significantly. I still use the Astra blades(they work well with the glycerin soap, lasting up to 6 shaving sessions per blade), being much cheaper than Feather blades I do expect to run into some \\&quot;bad apples\\&quot; while using them, which I won&#x27;t feel bad about replacing instantly because they are cheaper(especially when compared to cartridges).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I developed my own shaving regimen for this razor. The neck area receives 3 passes(2 up and 1 down), the sideburns 2 passes(1 up and 1 down), mustache 2.5 passes(1 down, 1 across, and some spots receive half of an upward pass), the most tricky beard area receives 3-5 passes(1 down, several across and up). I rotate the razor to use both sides of the blade. This regimen leaves me with smooth skin for up to a day.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;One thing to note. It now takes me about 30 minutes to shave properly. I don&#x27;t do it in the morning, I shave in the evening before going to sleep(it helps to take a shower beforehand to soften the hairs and skin before shaving). This gives me the maximum amount of time to shave, because if you rush with DE razors you are more likely to cut yourself and leave behind some stubble.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The best part of Double Edge razors is that you do not feel like you are forced to conform to some Monopoly. You choose the blade you want to use, you choose the cream or soap you want to use, you choose the razor you want to use. What it could be called is \\&quot;open source\\&quot; shaving, like with computer software. I minimize the waste I produce - all I need to throw away are shaving soap packages(mostly paper) and used blades. I also purchased a Wilkinson Sword DE razor as an auxiliary razor.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I recommend the Feather Double Edge razor to beginners, but the Feather blades are not for me.</li>
    <li> I&#x27;ve been using this for about a year. I don&#x27;t use it very heavily since I only shave 2-3 times a week (I don&#x27;t mind the stubble and shaving more often tends to cause people in my family trouble) and it&#x27;s really only for shaving around my beard. That said, every time I use it, I take the blade out and rinse the whole thing and dry it thoroughly.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;It stands up really well to that sort of regular rigorous use of the butterfly mechanism and despite the steam from the shower, none of the parts of the razor have rusted. If I didn&#x27;t want to clean and dry it that way so often, I would probably be happier with a screw-together razor but I think this will hold together fine for at least another 2-3 years.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I didn&#x27;t care for the blades that came with it and was glad I bought a 100ct. of another brand for about $8 at the same time. The one star comes off because I think it would be better to offer the razor without the \\&quot;freebie\\&quot; blades and at a slightly lower price.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;At any rate, shaving this way is much nicer and quite a bit cheaper than the new fashioned way.</li>
    <li> I&#x27;ve been thinking about coming back to double edge shaving after my own experience. I, like most of my male brethren, have been led to the false conclusion by the grooming companies that \\&quot;more blades are better.\\&quot; I am here to tell you that is not the case. I&#x27;ll be 53 at the end of the month and my face is breaking out like it did when I was 14. Recently, I have been using 5 blade cartridges from Rite-Aid/CVS/Safeway that were inexpensive when compared to the big guys (about half price for the same count of cartridges) but that weren&#x27;t as high quality. I started with the Dollar Shave Club six blade (!) alternative last month. The cost for that is $9.00 plus shipping per month for 4 carts. They aren&#x27;t the best either, with a comfort strip that can barely survive 1 or 2 days and a dullness threshold that is shocking. Fortunately, with DSC, they come every month, so you can use them with some impunity.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;My face, however, continued to look like the surface of Mars. Last month, I pulled an ingrown hair from my left cheek. Needless to say, that was the last straw. After some searching on ebay and Amazon, I found this Feather double edge handle. One of the reviews here compares this handle favorably to the Gilette G1000 (The Knack). I learned on a Gilette adjustable shortly before converting to the Atra in 1977 and not looking back. I compare the Feather handle to that, except for the fact that the adjustable was not an agressive shave by any measure. I remember only nicking myself a couple of times in the two or three years of use I got out of it.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I used the Feather this morning for the first time, It looks cheap, believe me, it isn&#x27;t. The business end holds the blade perfectly and the butterfly exposes the blade just right. The handle is balanced and it is just heavy enough. If you are coming back to DE shaving, you won&#x27;t have any trouble finding the right angle to shave at. If you are a beginner, watch a couple of Mantic59&#x27;s YouTube videos to get the technique. I had a good first time, I did a two pass shave because when I shave every day, I have a light to moderate growth. Lately, I let myself go on the weekends (it gives my face a chance to recover) so on Monday, I generally have a heavy growth, and I can let you know then.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Let me also comment on the quality of the blades. These guys are sharp, certainly sharper than the Personas you get from CVS. I bought an extra 10 based on reviews ([[ASIN:B001G5FOLI 10 Feather Razor Blades NEW Hi-stainless Double Edge]]) and will report on them in an update.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I also picked up the [[ASIN:B004L4EING Van Der Hagen Men&#x27;s Luxury, Shave Set]] and it&#x27;s pretty good too. I&#x27;ll have a review of that over there.e technique. I had a good first time, I did a two pass shave because when I shave every day, I have a light to moderate growth.     <li> I bought this after my Edwin Jagger Razor broke. I figured I could save a few bucks. Despite being mostly made of plastic the build quality of the razor seems good. I came across a vintage badger hair brush at an antique store for $6. It outperforms the new $11 one by a significant margin.</li>
